But installation requires 8 manual steps including PostgreSQL server setup, and the database starts empty.\n27\t\n28\t**Comparison with arxiv-sanity-lite** (the project that inspired this one):\n29\t- arxiv-sanity-lite uses SQLite via `sqlitedict`, brute-force search (Python for-loop), per-request SVM over TF-IDF. Total deps: 5. Runs on a $5 VPS.\n30\t- Our project uses PostgreSQL with tsvector full-text search, async SQLAlchemy ORM, 8 migrations, 14+ dependencies. Feature-rich but heavy to install.\n31\t- arxiv-sanity-lite's architecture proves that SQLite + simple Python is sufficient for ~30K papers at the personal research tool scale.\n32\t\n33\t**PostgreSQL coupling analysis:**\n34\t- Full-text search (`tsvector`, `ts_rank_cd`, `websearch_to_tsquery`): 4 files, ~250 lines in `db/queries.py`\n35\t- JSONB columns: 7 uses across models (storage, not queried)\n36\t- `pg_insert` ON CONFLICT: 4 files (upsert pattern)\n37\t- `asyncpg` driver: referenced in 7 files via connection strings\n38\t- `ARRAY(String)`: 1 use (`category_list`)\n39\t- All have SQLite equivalents (FTS5, JSON text, INSERT OR REPLACE, aiosqlite, JSON arrays)\n40\t"}]},"uuid":"1e32c160-4745-437b-883a-78f01a357d6f","timestamp":"2026-04-02T09:34:13.912Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"3ab87dd6-3d61-42e8-a8d0-37258bf8acef","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/rookslog/workspace/projects/get-shit-done-reflect","sessionId":"cb3ee1b7-d088-4c0b-8949-e337c029701c","version":"2.1.90","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"greedy-finding-fog"}

At the same time, the project's own cybernetic synthesis argues against turning research infrastructure into a rigid automation machine that displaces human epistemic judgment.\n27\t\n28\tThe immediate design pressure is concrete: the user encounters high-value frontier material daily and wants a way to capture it, preserve provenance, and turn it into deep-dive inputs for research. The architectural pressure is also concrete: if the project simply \"grows capabilities\" without a bounded role, it risks becoming a generic R&D operating system whose memory and workflow structures pre-select inquiry too early. The indeterminate situation is therefore not \"should we add tools?\" but \"what kind of tool layer expands contact with frontier material without collapsing the project into platform sprawl or judgment automation?\"\n29\t\n30\t### Evidence Base\n31\t\n32\t<!--\n33\tCorroborated? column tracks whether claims survived falsification attempts (Step 2.5).\n34\tPer falsificationism: corroboration is provisional (\"survived our best attempt to falsify\"),\n35\tnot verification (which implies certainty no finite number of checks can establish).\n36\tSee philosophy: falsificationism/corroboration-not-confirmation.\n37\t\n38\tSignal ID column tracks whether evidence has been formalized as a KB signal.\n39\t- Formal signal: use the sig-YYYY-MM-DD-slug ID\n40\t- Created during deliberation: signal with source: deliberation-trigger"}]},"uuid":"5d9a71c9-5ca2-4172-b8e6-c1c055272695","timestamp":"2026-04-02T09:34:14.262Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"8e55701f-9da8-431a-8d86-c7aea332dc08","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/rookslog/workspace/projects/get-shit-done-reflect","sessionId":"cb3ee1b7-d088-4c0b-8949-e337c029701c","version":"2.1.90","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"greedy-finding-fog"}

{"parentUuid":"01879248-bb8b-44b5-9757-cff0a65bc10b","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"7ee03b9f-ea9f-4986-8bbb-2c6a90ad682e","agentId":"a31cd5011c42f68f9","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Y4bohT43RM49WMfyNNnGF9","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t---\n2\tname: gsd:deliberate\n3\tdescription: Start or continue a structured deliberation about a design question, grounded in signals and philosophical principles\n4\targument-hint: '\"topic\" | --continue <filename>'\n5\tallowed-tools:\n6\t  - Read\n7\t  - Write\n8\t  - Edit\n9\t  - Bash\n10\t  - Glob\n11\t  - Grep\n12\t  - AskUserQuestion\n13\t  - Agent\n14\t---\n15\t\n16\t<objective>\n17\tCreate or continue a structured deliberation document in `.planning/deliberations/`.\n18\t\n19\tDeliberations are the structured thinking between \"something seems off\" and \"here's what we'll do about it.\" They can be triggered by formal signals, but equally by conversation observations, user questions, or intuitions that haven't yet crystallized into named problems.\n20\t\n21\t**How it integrates with the pipeline:**\n22\t```\n23\tObservation (any source) → Deliberation (think) → Planning (plan) → Execution (build) →\n24\tVerification (check) → Signal Collection (observe) → Evaluation (compare predictions vs outcomes)\n25\t```\n26\t\n27\tDeliberations can enter the pipeline at any point — they don't require upstream signals. A user noticing \"why are all signals active?\" is a valid trigger, even though no signal says \"signals are all active.\" The deliberation process itself may discover or create signals as a byproduct.\n28\t</objective>\n29\t\n30\t<execution_context>\n31\t@~/.claude/get-shit-done/templates/deliberation.md\n32\t@~/.claude/get-shit-done/references/ui-brand.md\n33\t</execution_context>\n34\t\n35\t<context>\n36\tArguments: $ARGUMENTS\n37\t\n38\t@.planning/STATE.md\n39\t@.planning/config.json\n40\t</context>\n41\t\n42\t<process>\n43\t\n44\t## Mode Detection\n45\t\n46\tParse arguments to determine mode:\n47\t\n48\t**Continue mode** (`--continue <filename>` or `--continue <slug>`):\n49\t1. Find the deliberation file in `.planning/deliberations/`\n50\t2. Read its current state\n51\t3. Route based on status:\n52\t   - `open` → resume analysis, present current state, continue deliberation\n53\t   - `concluded` → offer to move to `adopted` (link implementation) or revise\n54\t   - `adopted` → offer to move to `evaluated` (check predictions) or revise\n55\t   - `evaluated` → present evaluation, offer supersession or closure\n56\t4. Skip to Step 6 (the conversational loop)\n57\t\n58\t**New mode** (topic string, no arguments, or mid-conversation):\n59\t1. If no arguments: check the current conversation for context first. The user may have been discussing something that naturally led here. Summarize what you understand the topic to be and confirm.\n60\t2. If arguments provided: use the topic string as the starting point.\n61\t3. Continue to Step 1.\n62\t\n63\t## Step 1: Identify the Trigger\n64\t\n65\t```\n66\t━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━\n67\t GSD ► DELIBERATION\n68\t━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━\n69\t```\n70\t\n71\tDeliberations can be triggered by many things. Identify which applies:\n72\t\n73\t| Trigger Type | Example | How to handle |\n74\t|-------------|---------|---------------|\n75\t| **Conversation observation** | \"Why are all signals active?\" / \"I noticed X seems odd\" | Extract the observation from conversation context. The deliberation IS the investigation. |\n76\t| **Formal signal** | \"Signal sig-2026-03-04-X needs a design response\" | Link signal IDs directly. |\n77\t| **Question about the system** | \"How does X work? Should it work differently?\" | The deliberation explores current state and whether change is warranted. |\n78\t| **Post-execution reflection** | \"Phase N revealed that our approach to X isn't working\" | Ground in execution artifacts. |\n79\t| **Intuition or unease** | \"Something feels wrong about how we handle Y\" | Valid trigger. Name the unease, then investigate. |\n80\t\n81\t**Capture the trigger** as a 1-2 sentence statement. This goes into the template's Trigger field.\n82\t\n83\tIf the trigger came from conversation (not explicit arguments), summarize what the conversation revealed and confirm with the user: \"It sounds like the deliberation topic is: {summary}. Is that right?\"\n84\t\n85\t## Step 1.5: Signal Gate\n86\t\n87\t**Purpose:** Observations that trigger deliberations are often signal-worthy themselves. Capturing them as formal signals before deliberating makes them traceable, referenceable by ID, and measurable for recurrence after intervention.\n88\t\n89\t**When this gate fires:** Trigger types: conversation observation, question about the system, intuition, or post-execution reflection. Skip for formal signal triggers (signals already exist).\n90\t\n91\t**How it works:**\n92\t\n93\t1. After the trigger is identified and (if applicable) verified against data in Step 2, assess whether the observation is signal-worthy. An observation is signal-worthy if it:\n94\t   - Reveals a systemic gap (not a one-off issue)\n95\t   - Would be valuable to track for recurrence after intervention\n96\t   - Could be missed by existing sensors (the user noticed it, the system didn't)\n97\t\n98\t2. If signal-worthy, offer to capture it:\n99\t\n100\t   \"This observation is worth tracking formally. Creating a signal makes it:\n101\t   - **Traceable** — future sessions can find it by ID\n102\t   - **Referenceable** — the deliberation links to it, not to ephemeral conversation\n103\t   - **Measurable** — we can check if it recurs after we address it\n104\t\n105\t   Create signal for: *'{observation summary}'*?\"\n106\t\n107\t   **AskUserQuestion guard:** If using AskUserQuestion for this offer, inspect the response for actual answer content. If the response contains no visible selection (e.g., \"User answered:\" with no option text), do NOT assume \"yes.\" Ask again in plain text or default to \"no\" (informal reference). See sig-2026-03-05-askuserquestion-phantom-answers for the known failure mode.\n108\t\n109\t3. If yes:\n110\t   - Write the signal file directly to `~/.gsd/knowledge/signals/{project}/` using the standard signal schema\n111\t   - Use `source: deliberation-trigger` to distinguish from sensor-detected or manual signals\n112\t   - Use appropriate `signal_type`: `capability-gap`, `epistemic-gap`, `deviation`, etc.\n113\t   - Rebuild index: `bash ~/.gsd/bin/kb-rebuild-index.sh`\n114\t   - Reference the signal ID in the deliberation's Evidence Base table (Signal ID column)\n115\t\n116\t4. If no: proceed with informal reference. Note `informal` in the Evidence Base Signal ID column.\n117\t\n118\t**During deliberation** (not just at entry):\n119\tAs the investigation in Steps 2-4 reveals additional findings, offer to capture those too. The deliberation process often discovers things the sensors missed. Batch if multiple: \"Investigation uncovered {N} additional findings worth tracking. Want me to create signals for them?\"\n120\t\n121\tEach signal created during deliberation gets `source: deliberation-trigger` and a tag linking it to the deliberation slug (e.g., `deliberation:signal-lifecycle-gap`).\n122\t\n123\t## Step 2: Surface Related Context\n124\t\n125\tGather relevant context — but treat each source as optional. Not every deliberation has related signals, prior deliberations, or relevant philosophy.\n126\t\n127\t**Scan for related signals** (best-effort):\n128\t- Read `~/.gsd/knowledge/index.md` if it exists\n129\t- Search for signals related to the topic (keyword match against signal summaries)\n130\t- If matches found: list top 5. If none: report \"No directly related signals found\" and move on.\n131\t- **Important:** The absence of signals can itself be informative. If the user noticed a systemic issue that no sensor detected, that's an epistemic gap worth noting.\n132\t\n133\t**Scan for prior deliberations** (best-effort):\n134\t- `ls .planning/deliberations/*.md` (exclude philosophy/ subdirectory)\n135\t- Check if any existing deliberation covers overlapping territory\n136\t- If none: move on.\n137\t\n138\t**Scan for relevant philosophy** (best-effort):\n139\t- Read `.planning/deliberations/philosophy/INDEX.md` if it exists\n140\t- List 2-3 most relevant philosophical principles. If no philosophy files exist: skip entirely.\n141\t\n142\t**Investigate the observation** (when trigger is conversation/intuition):\n143\t- If the user observed something about the system's state (e.g., \"all signals are active\"), investigate it. Run queries, read files, count things. Ground the observation in data before deliberating about it.\n144\t- Present what you found: \"You noticed X. I checked, and here's what the data shows: {findings}\"\n145\t\n146\tPresent findings (only sections that have content):\n147\t\n148\t```\n149\t## Related Context\n150\t\n151\t{### Observation Investigated — if trigger was conversation/intuition}\n152\t{What was checked and what the data shows}\n153\t\n154\t{### Active Signals ({N} related) — if any found}\n155\t{Table: ID | Severity | Summary}\n156\t\n157\t{### Prior Deliberations — if any found}\n158\t{List: filename | status | relevance}\n159\t\n160\t{### Philosophical Principles — if any found}\n161\t{List: cite key | principle | relevance}\n162\t\n163\t{### Epistemic Note — if no signals/deliberations found}\n164\t{Note what the absence means: \"No sensors have detected this pattern, suggesting it falls outside current sensor coverage.\"}\n165\t```\n166\t\n167\t## Step 2.5: Severe Testing\n168\t\n169\t<!--\n170\tGrounded pluralistically in:\n171\t- philosophy: error-statistics/severity-principle — a test is severe when it would\n172\t  probably detect the error if present (Mayo)\n173\t- philosophy: pragmatism/warranted-assertibility — claims are warranted through\n174\t  well-conducted inquiry, not through certainty (Dewey)\n175\t- philosophy: pragmatism/fallibilism — all claims are provisional and subject to\n176\t  revision (Peirce)\n177\t- Falsificationism contributes the asymmetry insight: look for disconfirming\n178\t  evidence specifically (Popper) — but the full Popperian programme is not\n179\t  required or assumed\n180\t\n181\tThis step exists because the first dog-food of this skill (2026-03-04) produced\n182\ttwo false factual claims that went unchallenged into the Analysis section. The\n183\tclaims would have been caught by reading two files. See:\n184\tsig-2026-03-04-deliberation-skill-lacks-epistemic-verification\n185\t-->\n186\t\n187\t**Purpose:** Before the Situation section becomes the basis for analysis, subject every factual claim to inquiry that would probably detect errors if present (Mayo's severity principle). This is not verification (which implies certainty no finite process can establish) but inquiry into whether claims are warranted (Dewey) — with specific attention to disconfirming evidence (Popper's asymmetry insight). Claims that survive are provisionally warranted, not confirmed.\n188\t\n189\t**Process:**\n190\t\n191\t1. **Extract claims.** List every factual claim in the Situation section that asserts something about the codebase, system state, or history. Include claims inherited from the trigger or from prior deliberation summaries.\n192\t\n193\t2. **For each claim, formulate the most direct falsification test:**\n194\t   - \"No automation exists for X\" → Search for code that does X (`Grep` for key terms, `Read` relevant workflow/agent files)\n195\t   - \"Feature Y was never built\" → Search for feature Y in the codebase\n196\t   - \"N things are in state Z\" → Query the data source directly\n197\t   - \"Previous deliberation concluded W\" → Read the deliberation file\n198\t\n199\t3. **Execute the test** using tool calls (Grep, Read, Bash). Do not reason about whether the claim is probably true — check.\n200\t\n201\t4. **Record the result** in the Evidence Base table:\n202\t   - **Corroborated:** The claim survived the falsification attempt. Note what was checked.\n203\t   - **Falsified:** The claim was disproven. Correct the Situation section immediately. Note what the evidence actually shows and how the initial claim was wrong.\n204\t   - **Inconclusive:** The test didn't definitively support or refute the claim. Note the ambiguity.\n205\t\n206\t5. **If any claims are falsified:** Pause and re-examine the framing. False premises may have shaped the core question. The corrected understanding may point to a different — and more precise — problem.\n207\t\n208\t**The Evidence Base table uses \"Corroborated?\" not \"Verified?\"** — because corroboration is provisional (\"survived our best attempt to falsify\") while verification implies certainty. Per Popper: no finite number of checks can verify a universal claim. See `philosophy: falsificationism/corroboration-not-confirmation`.\n209\t\n210\t**Anti-pattern to avoid:** Reading one file that supports the claim and stopping. This is confirmation bias — finding one supporting datum and treating it as sufficient. Per Mayo: a test with low severity (the claim would probably pass even if false) provides no evidence. Design tests that probe the claim's weakest point — where it is most likely to be wrong.\n211\t\n212\t**What makes a test severe (Mayo):** A test is severe when the probability of the claim passing it, given that the claim is false, is low. \"Grep found nothing\" is moderately severe (the feature would likely use the expected name). \"Code exists in the workflow spec\" is less severe for the claim \"the automation works\" (code existing doesn't mean it executes). \"The output artifact shows the state change\" is more severe (directly probes whether the transition fired).\n213\t\n214\t## Step 3: Frame the Question\n215\t\n216\tAsk the user to refine the framing:\n217\t\n218\t\"Based on the context above, here's how I'd frame the core question:\n219\t\n220\t**{Draft core question}**\n221\t\n222\tIs this the right framing, or is there a deeper question underneath?\"\n223\t\n224\tUse AskUserQuestion with options:\n225\t- \"That framing works\" (proceed)\n226\t- \"The real question is...\" (refine)\n227\t- \"Let me explain more context first\" (gather more)\n228\t\n229\t## Step 4: Create the File\n230\t\n231\tGenerate the deliberation file from the template:\n232\t- **Filename:** `.planning/deliberations/{slug}.md` where slug is kebab-case from topic\n233\t- **Populate:** Date, trigger (from conversation context), affects (from related phases/requirements), related (from context scan)\n234\t- **Fill Situation section** with the corroborated evidence base from Steps 2-2.5\n235\t- **Fill Framing section** with the agreed core question\n236\t- **Note any falsified claims** in the Situation section with corrections\n237\t\n238\tWrite the file. Report:\n239\t```\n240\tCreated: .planning/deliberations/{slug}.md\n241\tStatus: Open\n242\tClaims tested: {N tested}, {N corroborated}, {N falsified}\n243\t```\n244\t\n245\t## Step 5: Explore the Design Space\n246\t\n247\tThis is the core deliberation loop.\n248\t\n249\t**Before proposing options, check prior deliberations:**\n250\t- Re-read the prior deliberations surfaced in Step 2\n251\t- For each one that covers overlapping territory, extract: what was already designed, what was already built, what gaps remain\n252\t- Present a summary: \"Prior deliberations have already addressed aspects of this problem: {summary}. The remaining gap is: {gap}.\"\n253\t- This prevents re-exploring design space that has already been covered — and prevents making claims about what exists without checking (the failure mode this step was created to prevent)\n254\t\n255\tFor each option worth considering:\n256\t\n257\t1. **Present the option** with Toulmin structure (claim, grounds, warrant, rebuttal)\n258\t2. **Ensure the grounds are corroborated** — if an option's grounds include factual claims about the codebase, check them (Step 2.5 discipline applies throughout, not just at the start)\n259\t3. **Ask the user** to react — agree, challenge, propose alternative\n260\t4. **Record tensions** — where do options conflict? What trade-offs exist?\n261\t\n262\tUse AskUserQuestion for structured choices. Use open conversation for nuanced discussion.\n263\t\n264\t**Important:** Do NOT converge too quickly. The value of deliberation is exploring the space, not rushing to a conclusion. Present at least 2 substantively different options before asking which direction to take.\n265\t\n266\t## Step 6: Record Predictions\n267\t\n268\tBefore concluding, record falsifiable predictions (per `philosophy: falsificationism/falsifiable-predictions`):\n269\t\n270\t\"If we go with Option {X}, what should we observe? Let me propose some predictions — tell me which are right and what I'm missing.\"\n271\t\n272\tPresent 2-4 candidate predictions with:\n273\t- What should happen (the bold conjecture)\n274\t- When/how we'd check (the severe test)\n275\t- What would prove the prediction wrong (the falsification condition)\n276\t\n277\t**Predictions must be specific enough to be falsifiable.** \"Things will improve\" is not a prediction. \"The number of signals stuck in 'detected' state will decrease by >50% within 2 phases\" is. Per Popper: bold conjectures that risk being wrong carry more epistemic content than timid ones that are compatible with any outcome.\n278\t\n279\t## Step 7: Conclude or Leave Open\n280\t\n281\tAsk the user:\n282\t- \"Ready to conclude with a recommendation?\" → Fill Recommendation section, set status to `concluded`\n283\t- \"Leave open for more thinking\" → Save current state, status stays `open`\n284\t- \"Need to investigate further first\" → Note open questions, suggest next steps (spike, research, etc.)\n285\t\n286\t## Step 8: Link to Pipeline\n287\t\n288\tIf concluded, offer integration points:\n289\t\n290\t\"This deliberation is concluded. To connect it to the pipeline:\"\n291\t\n292\t- **Reference in planning:** \"When running `/gsd:plan-phase`, mention this deliberation — the planner will read it\"\n293\t- **Capture as requirement:** \"Should any conclusions become formal requirements in REQUIREMENTS.md?\"\n294\t- **Link signals:** \"Should I update STATE.md to note which signals this addresses?\"\n295\t\n296\tIf the deliberation responds to specific signals, note the signal IDs in the Decision Record section.\n297\t\n298\t## Step 9: Save and Report\n299\t\n300\tUpdate the file with all content from the conversation. Commit if `commit_docs` is true:\n301\t\n302\t```bash\n303\tCOMMIT_DOCS=$(cat .planning/config.json 2>/dev/null | grep -o '\"commit_docs\"[[:space:]]*:[[:space:]]*[^,}]*' | grep -o 'true\\|false' || echo \"true\")\n304\tgit check-ignore -q .planning 2>/dev/null && COMMIT_DOCS=false\n305\t```\n306\t\n307\tIf commit: `git add .planning/deliberations/{file} && git commit -m \"docs(deliberation): {slug}\"`\n308\t\n309\tReport:\n310\t```\n311\t───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n312\t\n313\t## Deliberation: {Title}\n314\t\n315\t**Status:** {open|concluded}\n316\t**File:** .planning/deliberations/{slug}.md\n317\t**Signals referenced:** {N}\n318\t**Predictions recorded:** {N}\n319\t\n320\t───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n321\t```\n322\t\n323\t</process>\n324\t\n325\t<evaluation_mode>\n326\t\n327\t## Evaluating a Previous Deliberation\n328\t\n329\tWhen continuing a deliberation in `adopted` status (implementation exists):\n330\t\n331\t1. **Read the predictions** from the Predictions section\n332\t2. **Check each prediction** against current codebase state:\n333\t   - Search for signal recurrence (related signals in KB post-implementation)\n334\t   - Check verification reports for the implementing phase\n335\t   - Read SUMMARY.md files from implementing plans\n336\t3. **Fill the Evaluation section:**\n337\t   - Match predictions against outcomes\n338\t   - Assess progressive vs degenerating (Lakatos)\n339\t   - Record lessons for future deliberations\n340\t4. **Set status to `evaluated`**\n341\t5. **Optionally create a signal** if the evaluation reveals something surprising (positive or negative)\n342\t\n343\tThis closes the loop: signals → deliberation → intervention → prediction → evaluation → new signals.\n344\t\n345\t</evaluation_mode>\n346\t\n347\t<workflow_integration>\n348\t\n349\t## Where Deliberation Fits in GSD Workflows\n350\t\n351\t**Upstream consumers (who reads deliberations):**\n352\t- `/gsd:plan-phase` — planner reads deliberations referenced in CONTEXT.md or ROADMAP.md\n353\t- `/gsd:discuss-phase` — creates CONTEXT.md which can reference deliberation conclusions\n354\t- `/gsd:reflect` — reflector can reference deliberation predictions when evaluating signal patterns\n355\t\n356\t**Downstream triggers (what triggers deliberation):**\n357\t- **Conversation observation:** User notices something odd, asks a question, or expresses unease about system behavior — no formal signal required\n358\t- **Signal accumulation:** Signal collection reveals recurring patterns with no existing response\n359\t- **Verification gaps:** Phase verification finds gaps that need design thinking before gap closure\n360\t- **Reflection output:** Reflector produces lessons that suggest architectural changes\n361\t- **Intuition:** \"Something feels wrong about X\" — valid trigger, investigation happens during deliberation\n362\t- **Post-execution:** Phase outcomes reveal that an approach isn't working as expected\n363\t\n364\t**State tracking:**\n365\t- STATE.md `Deliberation context:` field links to active deliberations\n366\t- ROADMAP.md phase details can reference deliberations in their description\n367\t- CONTEXT.md per-phase can include pointers to relevant concluded deliberations\n368\t\n369\t</workflow_integration>\n370\t\n371\t<design_notes>\n372\t- Deliberations are human-driven, system-supported (per deliberation-system-design.md)\n373\t- The system surfaces context and structures conversation; the human deliberates\n374\t- Template sections map to philosophical frameworks (noted in HTML comments)\n375\t- Predictions are the key innovation: they make deliberations falsifiable (Lakatos)\n376\t- Evaluation mode enables meta-learning about deliberation quality itself\n377\t- Step 2.5 (Severe Testing) structurally embodies falsificationism — not advisory (\"be rigorous\") but procedural (\"attempt to falsify each claim before proceeding\"). Added after first dog-food revealed false claims entering the analysis unchecked (sig-2026-03-04-deliberation-skill-lacks-epistemic-verification)\n378\t- Evidence Base uses \"Corroborated?\" not \"Verified?\" — verification implies certainty; corroboration is provisional (philosophy: falsificationism/corroboration-not-confirmation)\n379\t- Prior Deliberation Check in Step 5 prevents re-exploring already-covered design space\n380\t- AskUserQuestion phantom answer guard in Signal Gate prevents acting on empty tool responses\n381\t</design_notes>\n382\t"}]},"uuid":"ab24c974-3b3e-4662-8d94-bd51ef9ab04c","timestamp":"2026-04-02T09:34:17.702Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"01879248-bb8b-44b5-9757-cff0a65bc10b","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/rookslog/workspace/projects/get-shit-done-reflect","sessionId":"cb3ee1b7-d088-4c0b-8949-e337c029701c","version":"2.1.90","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"greedy-finding-fog"}

GAPS & STALENESS ANALYSIS\n\n**Staleness:**\n- March 5-6 deliberations (6 files) unmodified for 28 days\n- No concluded deliberation has progressed to \"evaluated\" status\n- v1.17-plus-roadmap-deliberation was revised once (2026-03-28 v1.18 update appended), but no other revisions observed\n- Open deliberations from March 20+ show recent activity, but earlier cohort is dormant\n\n**Structural gaps identified in open deliberations themselves:**\n\n1. **deliberation-frontmatter-provenance-and-workflow-consumption.md** (open): \"Deliberations can remain open and relevant across phases, but the current workflow treats them as manually discovered prose.\"\n\n2. **deliberation-revision-lineage-and-citation-stability.md** (open): \"Once deliberations become routable and roadmap-relevant, the framework needs a principled way to revise them without silently rewriting project memory.\"\n\n3. **deliberation-workflow-stratification-and-research-routing.md** (open): \"Some deliberations are exploratory, some resolve design choices, some are interpretive. These should not all be treated under one workflow.\"\n\n4. **sensor-expansion-and-harness-integration-gaps.md** (open): Notes that 12 sensors ran but were absent from model profiles — integration gap between deliberations and feature infrastructure.\n\n**These open deliberations identify gaps in the deliberation system itself** — a meta-deliberation problem that the system hasn't solved.\n\n---\n\n### 9. USAGE PATTERNS THAT DIFFER FROM INTENDED WORKFLOW\n\n**GSD Reflect actual pattern:** Documentation + reference, not workflow\n\n- Deliberations are stored, cited in research contexts, but not automatically surfaced\n- Planning workflows that should reference them (plan-phase) do not have a \"Find related deliberations\" step\n- Discussion workflows (discuss-phase) create CONTEXT.md but no automation to pull in relevant concluded deliberations\n- Result: Planners must manually remember to check .planning/deliberations/ for relevant prior thinking\n\n**Cross-project pattern:** Lightweight, scope-focused\n\n- arxiv-sanity-mcp uses them for feature scope (v2-literature-review-features is about v2 planning)\n- zlibrary-mcp uses one for v1.2 milestone scope decision\n- epistemic-agency uses them for project role definition and milestone architecture\n- None show the deep, signal-grounded, falsifiable-prediction-oriented pattern that GSD Reflect intends\n\n**What should happen but doesn't:**\n\n- [ ] A new phase should automatically list relevant open/concluded deliberations from .planning/deliberations/\n- [ ] Signal collection should feed back into deliberation evaluation (check predictions)\n- [ ] Deliberations should have explicit lifecycle: open → concluded → adopted → evaluated → archived/superseded\n- [ ] Deliberation types should route to different workflows (exploratory vs design vs scope)\n- [ ] Philosophical principles should be checked during deliberation (not just cited in headers)\n\n---\n\n### 10. EVIDENCE THAT DELIBERATIONS WORK (WHEN THEY WORK)\n\n**High-engagement deliberations:**\n\n1. **spike-epistemic-rigor-and-framework-reflexivity.md** (open): Evidence of deep signal integration (sig-2026-03-20-premature-spike-decisions, sig-2026-03-20-spike-experimental-design-rigor, sig-2026-03-20-jaccard-screening-methodology, sig-2026-03-19-spike-framework-scope-gap). Cross-project (arrows-sanity-mcp spike artifacts referenced). Strong evidence base with comparison tables.\n\n2. **pre-v1.19-session-capture.md** (open, just created 2026-04-02): Explicitly documents 7 threads from extended deliberation session. References epistemic-agency knowledge base (154 papers, 47 findings). Identifies research-grounding need and links to other projects' work.\n\n3. **self-improvement-pipeline-design.md** (concluded): References 3 other deliberations, 4 signal patterns, and 3 philosophy frameworks. The Evidence Base section has a detailed verification trace. This is the intentional design.\n\n**What makes these work:**\n- Active conversation during creation (not written then abandoned)\n- Signal integration via trigger_signals field\n- Cross-referencing to other deliberations\n- Philosophy framework citations\n- Evidence base with corroboration column\n- Explicit design space exploration with named options\n\n---\n\n### 11. SUMMARY: ACTUAL VS INTENDED\n\n**Intended deliberation system:** Structured design thinking between signal detection and planning, with predictions that get evaluated, philosophy as active constraint, and automatic surfacing of relevant prior work.\n\n**Actual deliberation system:** Documentation layer that captures important conversations and design decisions, which planners can manually consult. Philosophy well-documented but not active in process. Predictions recorded but never evaluated.\n\n**Positive aspects:**\n- Deliberation creation triggers are working (signal + conversation observation both work)\n- Signal integration happening (trigger_signals, signal-sourced tags in KB)\n- Philosophy framework is comprehensive and well-indexed\n- Cross-project design thinking (epistemic-agency synthesis flowing into arxiv-sanity-mcp and GSD Reflect)\n- Deliberations DO influence planning when cited explicitly\n\n**Gaps:**\n- **Evaluation gap:** Predictions not checked against outcomes\n- **Staleness:** March deliberations untouched for 28 days\n- **Routing gap:** No automatic \"surface relevant deliberations\" during planning\n- **Type gap:** Deliberations not stratified (exploratory vs design vs scope deliberations use same workflow)\n- **Integration gap:** 32 deliberations exist but most are read manually, not by automation\n- **Citation stability:** deliberation-revision-lineage-and-citation-stability.md is open — the system itself knows this is unresolved\n- **Feature disconnect:** Deliberations mention sensor gaps, but sensor-expansion-and-harness-integration-gaps.md shows deliberations aren't pulling into feature builds\n\n---\n\n### 12. RECOMMENDATIONS (EVIDENCE-BASED)\n\n**Immediate:**\n1. **Evaluate one concluded deliberation.** Pick `signal-lifecycle-closed-loop-gap` (oldest, should have visible outcomes). Create Evaluation section comparing Phase 39-43 outcomes to recorded predictions. Publish findings.\n2. **Create a deliberation routing agent.** Add to discuss-phase: \"Searching for related deliberations...\" → list open + concluded deliberations by topic. Make it opt-in first, measure uptake.\n3. **Archive stale deliberations.** March 5-6 deliberations unmodified for 28 days. Move to `.planning/deliberations/archive/` and note why.\n\n**Medium-term (1-2 weeks):**\n4. **Implement deliberation-workflow-stratification-and-research-routing.md.** This open deliberation identifies the design space for different deliberation types. Complete it and implement routing.\n5. **Add evaluation mode to skill lifecycle.** When /gsd:deliberate is called on a concluded deliberation, require evaluation before any new work.\n6. **Link sensor expansion back to deliberations.** sensor-expansion-and-harness-integration-gaps.md identifies sensor gaps; create a phase that updates model-profiles.cjs and agent specs per that deliberation's recommendations.\n\n**Longer-term (v1.19+):**\n7. **Philosophy as active process.** During deliberation Step 5 (design space exploration), require engagement with 1-2 relevant philosophical principles per option (not just headers).\n8. **Cross-project deliberation routing.** epistemic-agency findings should automatically trigger review of arxiv-sanity-mcp and GSDR deliberations.\n9. **Deliberation predictive power dashboard.** Track: predictions recorded → outcomes checked → accuracy over time.
